class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eIntroduction: PhysiCell's MultiCellular Data Standard (MCDS) Time Step Anatomy\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-introduction-physicells-multicellular-data-standard-mcds-time-step-anatomy\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Introduction: PhysiCell's MultiCellular Data Standard (MCDS) Time Step Anatomy\" href=\"#introduction-physicells-multicellular-data-standard-mcds-time-step-anatomy\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eEach time PhysiCell's internal time tracker passes a time step where data is to be saved, it generates a number of files of various types.\u003cbr\u003e\nEach of these files will have a number at the end that indicates where it belongs in the sequence of outputs.\u003cbr\u003e\nAll files from the first round of output will end in 00000000.*, and the second round will be 00000001.*, and so on.\u003cbr\u003e\nHave a look at this \u003ca href=\"https://github.com/elmbeech/physicelldataloader/tree/master/pcdl/data_timeseries_2d\"\u003ePhysiCell data time series\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eLet's assume we captured data every simulation time hour, and we're interested in the set of output half a day through the run, the 13th set of output files.\u003cbr\u003e\nThe files we care about most from this set consists of:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eoutput00000012.xml\u003c/strong\u003e: This file is the main organizer of the data.\nIt contains an overview of the data stored in the MultiCellDS as well as some actual data, including:\u003cbr\u003e\nmetadata (MultiCellDS version, PhysiCell or BioFVM version, simulation time, runtime, and processing time stamp),\u003cbr\u003e\ncoordinates for the computational domain (mesh),\u003cbr\u003e\nparameters for diffusing substrates in the microenvironment (continuum_variables),\u003cbr\u003e\ncolumn labels and units for the cell data (cell_population),\u003cbr\u003e\nfile names for the files that contain microenvironment and cell data at this time step (mat and possibly graph.txt files),\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eoutput00000012_cells.mat\u003c/strong\u003e: This is a MATLAB matrix file that contains tracked information about the individual cells in the model.\nIt tells us things like the cells' position, volume, secretion, cell cycle status, and user defined cell parameters.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eoutput00000012_microenvironment0.mat\u003c/strong\u003e: This is a MATLAB matrix file that contains data about the microenvironment at this time step.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe Legacy Way to Run pyMCDS\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-the-legacy-way-to-run-pymcds\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: The Legacy Way to Run pyMCDS\" href=\"#the-legacy-way-to-run-pymcds\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIn the early days, PhysiCell output was with the help of a script loaded into MATLAB for analysis.\u003cbr\u003e\nIn 2019, a similar loader script was written for phython3.\nThe name of this script filed was pyMCDS.py.\nTo load data, this file was copied into the PhysiCell root or output folder.\nA python3 shell was fired up in the directory where this file resisted, and the pyMCDS class was loaded with this code line below.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"# legacy way to load the pyMCDS class\nfrom pyMCDS import pyMCDS\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e# legacy way to load the pyMCDS class\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003efrom\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003epyMCDS\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eimport\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003epyMCDS\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIn autumn 2022 an endeavor was undertaken to pack this pyMCDS.py script into a pip installable python3 library and develop it further, but always in such a way that, if necessary, the code could still be run like in the early days.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAll this resulted in the PhysiCell data loader (pcdl) library here.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIf you inspect today's pcdl source code, you will see that the \u003ca href=\"https://raw.githubusercontent.com/elmbeech/physicelldataloader/master/pcdl/pyMCDS.py\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003epyMCDS.py\u003c/a\u003e file still exists.\nAnd if you feel so, it is still possible to load PhysiCell output the ancient way!\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003ethe pyMCDS class as such evolved into the TimeStep class, which is more powerful although it has heavier library dependencies too.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 related to the snapshot is loaded.\u003cbr\u003e\nFor speed and less memory usage, it is however possible to only load the essential (output xml and cell mat data), and exclude microenvironment, graph voxel.\u003cbr\u003e\nIt is common, but not necessary, that the voxel's width, height, and depth is the same.\u003cbr\u003e\nHowever, you will find that in this test dataset this is not the case. \u003cbr\u003e\nIn the related \u003ccode\u003ePhysiCell_settings.xml\u003c/code\u003e file the voxel was specified as 30[nm] high, 20[nm] wide, and 10[nm] deep.\u003cbr\u003e\nWe can retrieve this voxel spacing value and voxel volume. \u003cbr\u003e\nAdditionally, we can retrieve the mesh spacing.\u003cbr\u003e\nYou will notice that voxel and mesh spacing values differ.\u003cbr\u003e\nThis is because this data set is from a 2D simulation. For that reason, the mesh depth is set to 1.\u003cbr\u003e\nIn 3D simulation data, voxel and mesh spacing will be the same because voxel and mesh depth is the same.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"mcds.get_mesh_spacing()  # [30.0, 20.0, 1]\nmcds.get_voxel_spacing() # [30.0, 20.0, 10.0]\nmcds.get_voxel_volume()  # 30[nm] * 20[nm] * 10[nm] = 6000[nm\\*\\*3]\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan 6000[nm\\*\\*3]\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eSince version 3, coordinate labels are distinct:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003ex,y,z:\u003c/strong\u003e stand for cell position coordinates, and are real values.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003em,n,p:\u003c/strong\u003e stand for mesh center coordinates, and are real values.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003ei,j,k:\u003c/strong\u003e stand for voxel index coordinates, and are unsigned integer values.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eFor a better understanding, let's fetch start and stop range values for each coordinate type.\u003cbr\u003e\nUnlike in the python range function, not only the start value, but also the stop value is inclusive.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"mcds.get_voxel_ijk_range()  # [(0, 10), (0, 10), (0, 0)]\nmcds.get_mesh_mnp_range()  # [(-15.0, 285.0), (-10.0, 190.0), (0.0, 0.0)]\nmcds.get_xyz_range()  # [(-30.0, 300.0), (-20.0, 200.0), (-5.0, 5.0)]\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003emcds\u003c/span\u003e.\u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003eget_voxel_ijk_range\u003c/span\u003e() class=\"pl-s1\"\u003emcds\u003c/span\u003e.\u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003eget_xyz_range\u003c/span\u003e()  \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e# [(-30.0, 300.0), (-20.0, 200.0), (-5.0, 5.0)]\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe domain benchmarks are:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003evoxel index values stretch from 0 to 10 longitude (i), 0 to 10 latitude (j), the 2D domain is only 1 voxel deep (k).\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003emesh center values stretch from -15[nm] to 285[nm] longitude (m), -10[nm] to 190[nm] latitude (n), and the depth mesh center (p) is at zero.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003ecells can hold a positioned between -30[nm] and 300[nm] longitude (x), -20[nm] and 200[nm] latitude (y), and -5[nm] and 5[nm] depth (z).\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eFor voxel and mesh centers, we can fetch the axis tick lists.\u003cbr\u003e\nEach of this function will return a list of 3 numpy arrays, ordered by ijk or mnp, respective.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"mcds.get_voxel_ijk_axis()\nmcds.get_mesh_mnp_axis()\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003emcds\u003c/span\u003e.\u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003eget_voxel_ijk_axis\u003c/span\u003e()\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003emcds\u003c/span\u003e.\u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003eget_mesh_mnp_axis\u003c/span\u003e()\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWe can even retrieve all mnp mesh center coordinate triplets, and the meshgrids in 2D or 3D shape itself.\u003cbr\u003e\nThe coordinate triplets are returned as numpy array.\u003cbr\u003e\nThe meshgrids are returned as a 3 way tensor (2D) or 4 way tensor (3D) numpy array. \u003cbr\u003e\nAs shown below, it is easy to subset these tensors.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003ea \u003cstrong\u003enumpy array\u003c/strong\u003e of all substrate concentrations at a particular xyz coordinate, ordered alphabetically by substrate name, like the list retrieved by the get_substrate_names function.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003esubstrate specific 3D or 2D \u003cstrong\u003emeshgrid numpy arrays\u003c/strong\u003e.\nTo get a 2D meshgrids you can slice though any z stack value, the function will always pick the closest mesh center coordinate, the smaller coordinate, if you hit the saddle point between two voxels.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003ematplotlib contour and contourf plots\u003c/strong\u003e, for any substrate, through any z_slice.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003ea and cell data can be retrieved as pandas datafarme, basic plotting (line plot, bar plot, histogram, boxplot, kernel density estimation plot, area plot, pie plot, scatter plot, hexbin plot) can easily be generated with the \u003cstrong\u003epandas plot function\u003c/strong\u003e.\nAs mentioned above, for microenvironment data, the TimeStep class has a mcds.get_contour function because pandas has no contour and contourf plots implementation.\nAll these plots are \u003cstrong\u003emathplotlib\u003c/strong\u003e plots, hence fine tuning can always be done using the matplotlib library.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://pandas.pydata.org/pandas-docs/stable/reference/api/pandas.DataFrame.plot.html\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003ehttps://pandas.pydata.org/pandas-docs/stable/reference/api/pandas.DataFrame.plot.html\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://matplotlib.org/\" tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eTransform an MCDS Time Step into an AnnData Object\u003c/h4\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-transform-an-mcds-time-step-into-an-anndata-object\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Transform an MCDS Time Step into an AnnData Object\" href=\"#transform-an-mcds-time-step-into-an-anndata-object\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe \u003ca href=\"https://anndata.readthedocs.io/en/latest/\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003eAnnData\u003c/a\u003e format is the de facto standard for single cell data analysis in python.\u003cbr\u003e\nIt is a one-liner to transform a mcds object onto an anndata object.\u003cbr\u003e\nThis is the gate to a whole new universe.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://scverse.org/\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003ehttps://scverse.org/\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"ann = mcds.get_anndata()\nprint(ann)  # AnnData object with n_obs × n_vars = 1099 × 80\n            #     obs: 'ID', 'current_phase', 'cycle_model'\n            #     obsm: 'spatial'\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003eann\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003emcds\u003c/span\u003e.\u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003eget_anndata\u003c/span\u003e()\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003eprint\u003c/span\u003e(\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003eann\u003c/span\u003e)  \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e# AnnData object with n_obs × n_vars = 1099 × 80\u003c/span\u003e\n            \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e#     obs: 'ID', 'current_phase', 'cycle_model'\u003c/span\u003e\n            \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e#     obsm: 'spatial'\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe output tells us that we have loaded a time step  with 1099 cells (agents) and 80 features.\nAnd that we have spatial coordinate annotation (position_x, position_y, position_z, time) of the loaded data.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWhatever you d'like to do with your physicell data, it most probably was already done with single cell wet lab data.\nThat's being said: PhysiCell data is different scdata than scRNA seq, for example.\nscRNA seq data is higher dimensional (e.g. for the human genome, over 20000 genes each time step) than PhysiCell data (tens, maybe hundreds of features).\nscRNA seq data is always single time step data because the measurement consumes the sample.\nPhysiCell data is always time series data, even we look at this moment only at one time step.\nThis all means, the wet lab bioinformatics will partially try to solve problems (e.g. trajectory inference), that simply are no problems for us and the other way around.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAnyhow, the gate is open.\nFor the shake of appearances, let's do a cluster analysis on PhysiCell output using scanpy.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"import scanpy as sc\n\n# loads only feature that have not the same value in all cells.\n# max absolute scales the features into a range between -1 and 1.\nann = mcds.get_anndata(states=2, scale='maxabs')\n\n# principal component analysis\nsc.tl.pca(ann)  # process anndata object with the pca tool.\nsc.pl.pca(ann)  # plot pca result.\nann.var_names  # list the numerical features we have at hand (alternative way: ann.var.index).\nann.obs_keys()  # list the categories features we have at hand (alternative way: ann.obs.columns).\nsc.pl.pca(ann, color=['current_phase','oxygen'])  # plot the pca results colored by some features.\nsc.pl.pca(ann, color=list(ann.var_names)+list(ann.obs_keys()))  # gotta catch 'em all!\nsc.pl.pca_variance_ratio(ann)  # plot how much of the variation each principal component captures.\n\n# neighborhood graph clustering\nsc.pp.neighbors(ann, n_neighbors=15)  # compute the neighborhood graph with the neighbors preprocess step.\nsc.tl.leiden(ann, resolution=0.01)  # cluster the neighborhood graph with the leiden tool.\nsc.pl.pca(ann, color='leiden')  # plot the pca results colored by leiden clusters.\n\n# umap dimensional reduction embedding\nsc.tl.umap(ann)  # process anndata object with the umap tool.\nsc.pl.umap(ann, color=['current_phase','oxygen','leiden'])  # plot the umap result colored by some features.\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eimport\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003escanpy\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eas\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003esc\u003c/span\u003e\n\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e# loads only feature that have not the same value in all cells.\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e# max absolute scales the features into a range between -1 and 1.\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003eann\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003emcds\u003c/span\u003e.\u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003eget_anndata\u003c/span\u003e(\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003estates\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e2\u003c/span\u003e, \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003escale\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e'maxabs'\u003c/span\u003e)\n\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e# principal component analysis\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003esc\u003c/span\u003e.\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003etl\u003c/span\u003e.\u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003epca\u003c/span\u003e(\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003eann\u003c/span\u003e)  \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e# process anndata object with the pca tool.\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003esc\u003c/span\u003e.\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003epl\u003c/span\u003e.\u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003epca\u003c/span\u003e(\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003eann\u003c/span\u003e)  \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e# plot pca result.\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003eann\u003c/span\u003e.\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003evar_names\u003c/span\u003e  \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e# list the numerical features we have at hand (alternative way: Contour Plot Images, and Movies\" href=\"#times-series-data-scatter-plot-images-contour-plot-images-and-movies\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWith PhysiCell it is not only possible to take data snapshots, but as well \u003ca href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SVG\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003esvg\u003c/a\u003e vector graphics images snapshots.\u003cbr\u003e\nPhysiCell's \u003ca href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Make_(software)\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003eMakefile\u003c/a\u003e has code to translate those svg images into \u003ca href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GIF\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003egif\u003c/a\u003e, \u003ca href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/JPEG\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003ejpeg\u003c/a\u003e, \u003ca href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Portable_Network_Graphics\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003epng\u003c/a\u003e, or \u003ca href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TIFF\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003etiff\u003c/a\u003e format, making use of the \u003ca href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ImageMagick\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003eimage magick\u003c/a\u003e library.\nThe Makefile also has  code to translate the jpeg, png, or tiff images into a \u003ca href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MP4_file_format\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003emp4\u003c/a\u003e movie, therefore utilizing the \u003ca href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FFmpeg\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003effmpeg\u003c/a\u003e library.\u003cbr\u003e\nTimeSeries instances provide similar functionality, although the jpeg, png, and tiff images are generated straight from data and not from the svg files.\nHowever, mp4 movies and gif images are generated in the same way.\nThis means the mcdsts.make_gif code will only run if image magick and mcdsts.make_movie code will only run if ffmpeg is installed on your computer.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"# fetch data\nmcdsts = pcdl.TimeSeries(s_path)\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e# fetch data\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003emcdsts\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003epcdl\u003c/span\u003e.\u003cspan class=\"pl-v\"\u003eTimeSeries\u003c/span\u003e(\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003es_path\u003c/span\u003e)\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eTranslate physicell output data into static raster graphic images:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"# cell images colored by cell_type\nmcdsts.make_imgcell()  # jpeg images colored by cell_type\nmcdsts.make_imgcell(ext='png')  # png images colored by cell_type\nmcdsts.make_imgcell(ext='tiff')  # tiff images colored by cell_type\n\n# cell images can be colored by any cell dataframe column, like, for example, by pressure\n# there are parameters to adjust cell size and more\nmcdsts.make_imgcell(focus='pressure')  # jpeg images colored by pressure values\n\n# substrate data owns an equivalent function,\n# being able to display any substrate dataframe column\nmcdsts.make_imgconc(focus='oxygen')  # jpeg images colored by oxygen values\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e# cell images colored by cell_type\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003eext\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e'tiff'\u003c/span\u003e)  \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e# tiff images colored class=\"pl-en\"\u003emake_imgcell\u003c/span\u003e(\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003efocus\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class="Box-sc-g0xbh4-0 eRvpKx"><div class="Box-sc-g0xbh4-0 cTsUqU js-snippet-clipboard-copy-unpositioned" data-hpc="true"><article class="markdown-body entry-content container-lg" itemprop="text"><div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h1 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">PhysiCell Data Loader Tutorial Man Page</h1><a id="user-content-physicell-data-loader-tutorial-man-page" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: PhysiCell Data Loader Tutorial Man Page" href="#physicell-data-loader-tutorial-man-page"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Please install the latest version of physicelldataloader (pcdl) branch v3,
as described in the <a href="https://github.com/elmbeech/physicelldataloader/blob/master/man/HOWTO.md">HowTo</a> section.<br>
Branch v1 and v2 exists mainly for backwards compatibility.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Tutorial - branch v1 and v2</h2><a id="user-content-tutorial---branch-v1-and-v2" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Tutorial - branch v1 and v2" href="#tutorial---branch-v1-and-v2"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">The original python-loader tutorial can be found here.</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><a href="http://www.mathcancer.org/blog/python-loader/" rel="nofollow">http://www.mathcancer.org/blog/python-loader/</a></li>
</ul>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Tutorial - branch v3</h2><a id="user-content-tutorial---branch-v3" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Tutorial - branch v3" href="#tutorial---branch-v3"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Introduction: PhysiCell's MultiCellular Data Standard (MCDS) Time Step Anatomy</h3><a id="user-content-introduction-physicells-multicellular-data-standard-mcds-time-step-anatomy" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Introduction: PhysiCell's MultiCellular Data Standard (MCDS) Time Step Anatomy" href="#introduction-physicells-multicellular-data-standard-mcds-time-step-anatomy"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Each time PhysiCell's internal time tracker passes a time step where data is to be saved, it generates a number of files of various types.<br>
Each of these files will have a number at the end that indicates where it belongs in the sequence of outputs.<br>
All files from the first round of output will end in 00000000.*, and the second round will be 00000001.*, and so on.<br>
Have a look at this <a href="https://github.com/elmbeech/physicelldataloader/tree/master/pcdl/data_timeseries_2d">PhysiCell data time series</a>.</p>
<p dir="auto">Let's assume we captured data every simulation time hour, and we're interested in the set of output half a day through the run, the 13th set of output files.<br>
The files we care about most from this set consists of:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><strong>output00000012.xml</strong>: This file is the main organizer of the data.
It contains an overview of the data stored in the MultiCellDS as well as some actual data, including:<br>
metadata (MultiCellDS version, PhysiCell or BioFVM version, simulation time, runtime, and processing time stamp),<br>
coordinates for the computational domain (mesh),<br>
parameters for diffusing substrates in the microenvironment (continuum_variables),<br>
column labels and units for the cell data (cell_population),<br>
file names for the files that contain microenvironment and cell data at this time step (mat and possibly graph.txt files),</li>
<li><strong>output00000012_cells.mat</strong>: This is a MATLAB matrix file that contains tracked information about the individual cells in the model.
It tells us things like the cells' position, volume, secretion, cell cycle status, and user defined cell parameters.</li>
<li><strong>output00000012_microenvironment0.mat</strong>: This is a MATLAB matrix file that contains data about the microenvironment at this time step.</li>
</ul>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">The Legacy Way to Run pyMCDS</h3><a id="user-content-the-legacy-way-to-run-pymcds" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: The Legacy Way to Run pyMCDS" href="#the-legacy-way-to-run-pymcds"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">In the early days, PhysiCell output was with the help of a script loaded into MATLAB for analysis.<br>
In 2019, a similar loader script was written for phython3.
The name of this script filed was pyMCDS.py.
To load data, this file was copied into the PhysiCell root or output folder.
A python3 shell was fired up in the directory where this file resisted, and the pyMCDS class was loaded with this code line below.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# legacy way to load the pyMCDS class
from pyMCDS import pyMCDS"><pre><span class="pl-c"># legacy way to load the pyMCDS class</span>
<span class="pl-k">from</span> <span class="pl-s1">pyMCDS</span> <span class="pl-k">import</span> <span class="pl-s1">pyMCDS</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">In autumn 2022 an endeavor was undertaken to pack this pyMCDS.py script into a pip installable python3 library and develop it further, but always in such a way that, if necessary, the code could still be run like in the early days.</p>
<p dir="auto">All this resulted in the PhysiCell data loader (pcdl) library here.</p>
<p dir="auto">If you inspect today's pcdl source code, you will see that the <a href="https://raw.githubusercontent.com/elmbeech/physicelldataloader/master/pcdl/pyMCDS.py" rel="nofollow">pyMCDS.py</a> file still exists.
And if you feel so, it is still possible to load PhysiCell output the ancient way!</p>
<p dir="auto">the pyMCDS class as such evolved into the TimeStep class, which is more powerful although it has heavier library dependencies too.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Loading an MCDS into Python3</h3><a id="user-content-loading-an-mcds-into-python3" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Loading an MCDS into Python3" href="#loading-an-mcds-into-python3"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">In this section, we will load the pcdl library and use its TimeStep class to load the data snapshot 00000012, described above, from <a href="https://github.com/elmbeech/physicelldataloader/tree/master/pcdl/data_timeseries_2d">data_timeseries_ 2d</a> from the 2D time series test dataset.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="import pathlib  # library to locate the test data
import pcdl  # the physicell data loader library

print('pcdl version:', pcdl.__version__)  # it is easy to figure out which pcdl version you run

pcdl.install_data()  # to install the test datasets

s_path = str(pathlib.Path(pcdl.__file__).parent.joinpath('data_timeseries_2d'))  # local path to the installed test data set
s_file = 'output00000012.xml'  # the snapshot we want to analyze
s_pathfile = f'{s_path}/{s_file}'
print('mcds xml:', s_pathfile)

# load mcds - multi cell data standard - object
mcds = pcdl.TimeStep(s_pathfile)  # loads the whole snapshot: the xml and all related mat and graph files"><pre><span class="pl-k">import</span> <span class="pl-s1">pathlib</span>  <span class="pl-c"># library to locate the test data</span>
<span class="pl-k">import</span> <span class="pl-s1">pcdl</span>  <span class="pl-c"># the physicell data loader library</span>

<span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">'pcdl version:'</span>, <span class="pl-s1">pcdl</span>.<span class="pl-s1">__version__</span>)  <span class="pl-c"># it is easy to figure out which pcdl version you run</span>

<span class="pl-s1">pcdl</span>.<span class="pl-en">install_data</span>()  <span class="pl-c"># to install the test datasets</span>

<span class="pl-s1">s_path</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-en">str</span>(<span class="pl-s1">pathlib</span>.<span class="pl-v">Path</span>(<span class="pl-s1">pcdl</span>.<span class="pl-s1">__file__</span>).<span class="pl-s1">parent</span>.<span class="pl-en">joinpath</span>(<span class="pl-s">'data_timeseries_2d'</span>))  <span class="pl-c"># local path to the installed test data set</span>
<span class="pl-s1">s_file</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s">'output00000012.xml'</span>  <span class="pl-c"># the snapshot we want to analyze</span>
<span class="pl-s1">s_pathfile</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s">f'<span class="pl-s1"><span class="pl-kos">{</span><span class="pl-s1">s_path</span><span class="pl-kos">}</span></span>/<span class="pl-s1"><span class="pl-kos">{</span><span class="pl-s1">s_file</span><span class="pl-kos">}</span></span>'</span>
<span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">'mcds xml:'</span>, <span class="pl-s1">s_pathfile</span>)

<span class="pl-c"># load mcds - multi cell data standard - object</span>
<span class="pl-s1">mcds</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">pcdl</span>.<span class="pl-v">TimeStep</span>(<span class="pl-s1">s_pathfile</span>)  <span class="pl-c"># loads the whole snapshot: the xml and all related mat and graph files</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Side note: for path, in general, unix (slash) and windows (backslash) notation will work.</p>
<p dir="auto">The legacy way of loading data, where filename and path had to be separated, works too.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# legacy way of loading a mcds object
mcds = pcdl.TimeStep('output00000012.xml', s_path)"><pre><span class="pl-c"># legacy way of loading a mcds object</span>
<span class="pl-s1">mcds</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">pcdl</span>.<span class="pl-v">TimeStep</span>(<span class="pl-s">'output00000012.xml'</span>, <span class="pl-s1">s_path</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">By default, all data related to the snapshot is loaded.<br>
For speed and less memory usage, it is however possible to only load the essential (output xml and cell mat data), and exclude microenvironment, graph data, and ID label mapping loading.<br>
Additionally, it is possible to specify for custom_data variable types other than the generic float type, namely: int, bool, and str.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# fine tuned way of loading a mcds object
mcds = pcdl.TimeStep(s_pathfile, custom_type={}, microenv=False, graph=False, settingxml=None)"><pre><span class="pl-c"># fine tuned way of loading a mcds object</span>
<span class="pl-s1">mcds</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">pcdl</span>.<span class="pl-v">TimeStep</span>(<span class="pl-s1">s_pathfile</span>, <span class="pl-s1">custom_type</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span>{}, <span class="pl-s1">microenv</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-c1">False</span>, <span class="pl-s1">graph</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-c1">False</span>, <span class="pl-s1">settingxml</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-c1">None</span>)</pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">The Loaded Data Structure</h3><a id="user-content-the-loaded-data-structure" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: The Loaded Data Structure" href="#the-loaded-data-structure"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# fetch data
mcds = pcdl.TimeStep(s_pathfile)"><pre><span class="pl-c"># fetch data</span>
<span class="pl-s1">mcds</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">pcdl</span>.<span class="pl-v">TimeStep</span>(<span class="pl-s1">s_pathfile</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">All loaded data lives in <code>mcds.data</code> dictionary.<br>
As in <strong>version 1</strong>, we have tried to keep everything organized inside this dictionary.<br>
Regarding <strong>version 1</strong>, the structure has slightly changed.<br>
However, in <strong>version 3</strong>, all data is accessible by functions. There should be no need to fetch data directly from the <code>mcds.data</code> dictionary!<br>
Anyhow, let's take a look at what we actually have in here.</p>
<p dir="auto"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="/elmbeech/physicelldataloader/blob/v3.2.13/man/img/physicelldataloader_data_dictionary_v3.2.2.png"><img src="/elmbeech/physicelldataloader/raw/v3.2.13/man/img/physicelldataloader_data_dictionary_v3.2.2.png" alt="mcds.data dictionary blueprint" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# main data branches
sorted(mcds.data.keys())  # metadata, mesh, substrate (continuum_variables), and agent (discrete_cells)

# metadata
sorted(mcds.data['metadata'].keys())  # multicellds version, physicell version, simulation time, runtime, time stamp, time unit, spatial unit, and substrate and cell type ID label mappings

# mesh
sorted(mcds.data['mesh'].keys())  # voxel (ijk), mesh (nmp), and position (xyz) range, axis, coordinate, grid objects, and voxel volume

# microenvironment
sorted(mcds.data['continuum_variables'].keys())  # list of all processed substrates, e.g. oxygen
sorted(mcds.data['continuum_variables']['oxygen'].keys())  # substrate related data values, unit, diffusion coefficient, and decay rate

# cell
sorted(mcds.data['discrete_cells'].keys())  # data, units, and graph dictionaries
sorted(mcds.data['discrete_cells']['data'].keys())  # all cell related, tracked data
sorted(mcds.data['discrete_cells']['units'].keys())  # all units from the cell related, tracked data
sorted(mcds.data['discrete_cells']['graph'].keys())  # neighbor_cells and attached_cells graph dictionaries"><pre><span class="pl-c"># main data branches</span>
<span class="pl-en">sorted</span>(<span class="pl-s1">mcds</span>.<span class="pl-s1">data</span>.<span class="pl-en">keys</span>())  <span class="pl-c"># metadata, mesh, substrate (continuum_variables), and agent (discrete_cells)</span>

<span class="pl-c"># metadata</span>

<span class="pl-c"># mesh</span>

<span class="pl-c"># microenvironment</span>
<span class="pl-en">sorted</span>(<span class="pl-s1">mcds</span>.<span class="pl-s1">data</span>[<span class="pl-s">'continuum_variables'</span>].<span class="pl-en">keys</span>())  <span class="pl-c"># list of all processed substrates, e.g. oxygen</span>
<span class="pl-en">sorted</span>(<span class="pl-s1">mcds</span>.<span class="pl-s1">data</span>[<span class="pl-s">'continuum_variables'</span>][<span class="pl-s">'oxygen'</span>].<span class="pl-en">keys</span>())  <span class="pl-c"># substrate related data values, unit, diffusion coefficient, and decay rate</span>

<span class="pl-c"># cell</span>
<span class="pl-en">sorted</span>(<span class="pl-s1">mcds</span>.<span class="pl-s1">data</span>[<span class="pl-s">'discrete_cells'</span>].<span class="pl-en">keys</span>())  <span class="pl-c"># data, units, and graph dictionaries</span>
<span class="pl-en">sorted</span>(<span class="pl-s1">mcds</span>.<span class="pl-s1">data</span>[<span class="pl-s">'discrete_cells'</span>][<span class="pl-s">'data'</span>].<span class="pl-en">keys</span>())  <span class="pl-c"># all cell related, tracked data</span>
<span class="pl-en">sorted</span>(<span class="pl-s1">mcds</span>.<span class="pl-s1">data</span>[<span class="pl-s">'discrete_cells'</span>][<span class="pl-s">'units'</span>].<span class="pl-en">keys</span>())  <span class="pl-c"># all units from the cell related, tracked data</span>
<span class="pl-en">sorted</span>(<span class="pl-s1">mcds</span>.<span class="pl-s1">data</span>[<span class="pl-s">'discrete_cells'</span>][<span class="pl-s">'graph'</span>].<span class="pl-en">keys</span>())  <span class="pl-c"># neighbor_cells and attached_cells graph dictionaries</span></pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Accessing the Loaded Data by the TimeStep Class Functions</h3><a id="user-content-accessing-the-loaded-data-by-the-timestep-class-functions" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Accessing the Loaded Data by the TimeStep Class Functions" href="#accessing-the-loaded-data-by-the-timestep-class-functions"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Once again, loud, for the ones in the back, in version 3, all data is accessible by functions.<br>
There should be no need to fetch data directly from the <code>mcds.data</code> dictionary of dictionaries.<br>
We will explore these functions in this section.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# fetch data
mcds = pcdl.TimeStep(s_pathfile)"><pre><span class="pl-c"># fetch data</span>
<span class="pl-s1">mcds</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">pcdl</span>.<span class="pl-v">TimeStep</span>(<span class="pl-s1">s_pathfile</span>)</pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Metadata</h4><a id="user-content-metadata" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Metadata" href="#metadata"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Fetch the data's MultiCellDS version, and the PhysiCell version the data was generated.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="mcds.get_multicellds_version()  # will return a string like MultiCellDS_2 or MultiCellDS_0.5
mcds.get_physicell_version()  # will return a string like PhysiCell_1.10.4 or BioFVM_1.1.7"><pre><span class="pl-s1">mcds</span>.<span class="pl-en">get_multicellds_version</span>()  <span class="pl-c"># will return a string like MultiCellDS_2 or MultiCellDS_0.5</span>
<span class="pl-s1">mcds</span>.<span class="pl-en">get_physicell_version</span>()  <span class="pl-c"># will return a string like PhysiCell_1.10.4 or BioFVM_1.1.7</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Fetch simulation time, runtime, and time stamp when the data was processed.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="mcds.get_time()   # will return a float value like 720.0
mcds.get_runtime()  # will return a float value like 15.596373
mcds.get_timestamp()  # will return a sting like 2022-10-19T01:12:01Z"><pre><span class="pl-s1">mcds</span>.<span class="pl-en">get_time</span>()   <span class="pl-c"># will return a float value like 720.0</span>
<span class="pl-s1">mcds</span>.<span class="pl-en">get_runtime</span>()  <span class="pl-c"># will return a float value like 15.596373</span>
<span class="pl-s1">mcds</span>.<span class="pl-en">get_timestamp</span>()  <span class="pl-c"># will return a sting like 2022-10-19T01:12:01Z</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Fetch substrate and cell type ID label mappings, read out from the PhysiCell_settings.xml file.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="mcds.get_substrate_dict()  # will return a dictionary, which maps substrate IDs to labels
mcds.get_celltype_dict()   # will return a dictionary, which maps cell type IDs to labels"><pre><span class="pl-s1">mcds</span>.<span class="pl-en">get_substrate_dict</span>()  <span class="pl-c"># will return a dictionary, which maps substrate IDs to labels</span>
<span class="pl-s1">mcds</span>.<span class="pl-en">get_celltype_dict</span>()   <span class="pl-c"># will return a dictionary, which maps cell type IDs to labels</span></pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Mesh Data</h4><a id="user-content-mesh-data" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Mesh Data" href="#mesh-data"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Let's start by the voxel.<br>
It is common, but not necessary, that the voxel's width, height, and depth is the same.<br>
However, you will find that in this test dataset this is not the case. <br>
In the related <code>PhysiCell_settings.xml</code> file the voxel was specified as 30[nm] high, 20[nm] wide, and 10[nm] deep.<br>
We can retrieve this voxel spacing value and voxel volume. <br>
Additionally, we can retrieve the mesh spacing.<br>
You will notice that voxel and mesh spacing values differ.<br>
This is because this data set is from a 2D simulation. For that reason, the mesh depth is set to 1.<br>
In 3D simulation data, voxel and mesh spacing will be the same because voxel and mesh depth is the same.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="mcds.get_mesh_spacing()  # [30.0, 20.0, 1]
mcds.get_voxel_spacing() # [30.0, 20.0, 10.0]
mcds.get_voxel_volume()  # 30[nm] * 20[nm] * 10[nm] = 6000[nm\*\*3]"><pre><span class="pl-s1">mcds</span>.<span class="pl-en">get_mesh_spacing</span>()  <span class="pl-c"># [30.0, 20.0, 1]</span>
<span class="pl-s1">mcds</span>.<span class="pl-en">get_voxel_spacing</span>() <span class="pl-c"># [30.0, 20.0, 10.0]</span>
<span class="pl-s1">mcds</span>.<span class="pl-en">get_voxel_volume</span>()  <span class="pl-c"># 30[nm] * 20[nm] * 10[nm] = 6000[nm\*\*3]</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Since version 3, coordinate labels are distinct:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><strong>x,y,z:</strong> stand for cell position coordinates, and are real values.</li>
<li><strong>m,n,p:</strong> stand for mesh center coordinates, and are real values.</li>
<li><strong>i,j,k:</strong> stand for voxel index coordinates, and are unsigned integer values.</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">For a better understanding, let's fetch start and stop range values for each coordinate type.<br>
Unlike in the python range function, not only the start value, but also the stop value is inclusive.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="mcds.get_voxel_ijk_range()  # [(0, 10), (0, 10), (0, 0)]
mcds.get_mesh_mnp_range()  # [(-15.0, 285.0), (-10.0, 190.0), (0.0, 0.0)]
mcds.get_xyz_range()  # [(-30.0, 300.0), (-20.0, 200.0), (-5.0, 5.0)]"><pre><span class="pl-s1">mcds</span>.<span class="pl-en">get_voxel_ijk_range</span>()  <span class="pl-c"># [(0, 10), (0, 10), (0, 0)]</span>
<span class="pl-s1">mcds</span>.<span class="pl-en">get_mesh_mnp_range</span>()  <span class="pl-c"># [(-15.0, 285.0), (-10.0, 190.0), (0.0, 0.0)]</span>
<span class="pl-s1">mcds</span>.<span class="pl-en">get_xyz_range</span>()  <span class="pl-c"># [(-30.0, 300.0), (-20.0, 200.0), (-5.0, 5.0)]</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">The domain benchmarks are:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>voxel index values stretch from 0 to 10 longitude (i), 0 to 10 latitude (j), the 2D domain is only 1 voxel deep (k).</li>
<li>mesh center values stretch from -15[nm] to 285[nm] longitude (m), -10[nm] to 190[nm] latitude (n), and the depth mesh center (p) is at zero.</li>
<li>cells can hold a positioned between -30[nm] and 300[nm] longitude (x), -20[nm] and 200[nm] latitude (y), and -5[nm] and 5[nm] depth (z).</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">For voxel and mesh centers, we can fetch the axis tick lists.<br>
Each of this function will return a list of 3 numpy arrays, ordered by ijk or mnp, respective.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="mcds.get_voxel_ijk_axis()
mcds.get_mesh_mnp_axis()"><pre><span class="pl-s1">mcds</span>.<span class="pl-en">get_voxel_ijk_axis</span>()
<span class="pl-s1">mcds</span>.<span class="pl-en">get_mesh_mnp_axis</span>()</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">We can even retrieve all mnp mesh center coordinate triplets, and the meshgrids in 2D or 3D shape itself.<br>
The coordinate triplets are returned as numpy array.<br>
The meshgrids are returned as a 3 way tensor (2D) or 4 way tensor (3D) numpy array. <br>
As shown below, it is easy to subset these tensors.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# all mnp coordinates
mnp_coordinats = mcds.get_mesh_coordinate()  # numpy array with shape (3, 121)
mnp_coordinats.shape  # (3, 121)

# 2D mesh grid
mn_meshgrid = mcds.get_mesh_2D()  # numpy array with shape (2, 11, 11)
mn_meshgrid.shape # (2, 11, 11)
m_meshgrid = mn_meshgrid[0]  # or explicit mn_meshgrid[0,:,:]
n_meshgrid = mn_meshgrid[1]  # or explicit mn_meshgrid[1,:,:]
m_meshgrid.shape  # (11, 11)
n_meshgrid.shape  # (11, 11)

# 3D mesh grid
mnp_meshgrid = mcds.get_mesh()  # numpy array with shape (3, 11, 11, 1)
mnp_meshgrid.shape # (3, 11, 11, 1)
m_meshgrid = mnp_meshgrid[0]  # or explicit mnp_meshgrid[0,:,:,:]
n_meshgrid = mnp_meshgrid[1]  # or explicit mnp_meshgrid[1,:,:,:]
p_meshgrid = mnp_meshgrid[2]  # or explicit mnp_meshgrid[2,:,:,:]
m_meshgrid.shape  # (11, 11, 1)
n_meshgrid.shape  # (11, 11, 1)
p_meshgrid.shape  # (11, 11, 1)"><pre><span class="pl-c"># all mnp coordinates</span>

<span class="pl-s1">n_meshgrid</span>.<span class="pl-s1">shape</span>  <span class="pl-c"># (11, 11)</span>

<span class="pl-c"># 3D mesh grid</span>
<span class="pl-s1">mnp_meshgrid</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">mcds</span>.<span class="pl-en">get_mesh</span>()  <span class="pl-c"># numpy array with shape (3, 11, 11, 1)</span>

<span class="pl-s1">n_meshgrid</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">mnp_meshgrid</span>[<span class="pl-c1">1</span>]  <span class="pl-c"># or explicit mnp_meshgrid[1,:,:,:]</span>
<span class="pl-s1">p_meshgrid</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">mnp_meshgrid</span>[<span class="pl-c1">2</span>]  <span class="pl-c"># or explicit mnp_meshgrid[2,:,:,:]</span>
<span class="pl-s1">m_meshgrid</span>.<span class="pl-s1">shape</span>  <span class="pl-c"># (11, 11, 1)</span>
<span class="pl-s1">n_meshgrid</span>.<span class="pl-s1">shape</span>  <span class="pl-c"># (11, 11, 1)</span>
<span class="pl-s1">p_meshgrid</span>.<span class="pl-s1">shape</span>  <span class="pl-c"># (11, 11, 1)</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Furthermore, there are two helper function.<br>
One to figure out if a particular xyz coordinate is still in side the mesh, another one to translate a xyz coordinate into ijk voxel indices.<br>
The translation function will by default checks if the given coordinate is in the mesh.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# is given xyz is in the mesh?
mcds.is_in_mesh(x=0, y=0, z=0)  # True
mcds.is_in_mesh(x=111, y=22, z=-5)  # True
mcds.is_in_mesh(x=111, y=22, z=-5.1)  # False and Warning @ pyMCDS.is_in_mesh : z = -5.1 out of bounds: z-range is (-5.0, 5.0)

# translate xyz into ijk!
mcds.get_voxel_ijk(x=0, y=0, z=0)  # [0,0,0]
mcds.get_voxel_ijk(x=111, y=22, z=-5)  # [4, 2, 0]
mcds.get_voxel_ijk(x=111, y=22, z=-5.1)  # None and Warning @ pyMCDS.is_in_mesh : z = -5.1 out of bounds: z-range is (-5.0, 5.0)"><pre><span class="pl-c"># is given xyz is in the mesh?</span>

<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Microenvironment (Continuum Variables) Data</h4><a id="user-content-microenvironment-continuum-variables-data" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Microenvironment (Continuum Variables) Data" href="#microenvironment-continuum-variables-data"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Let's have a look at the substrate.<br>
We can retrieve an alphabetically ordered list of all substrates processes in the simulation.<br>
In the loaded dataset, only one substrate, oxygen, was part of the simulation.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="mcds.get_substrate_names()  # ['oxygen']"><pre><span class="pl-s1">mcds</span>.<span class="pl-en">get_substrate_names</span>()  <span class="pl-c"># ['oxygen']</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">We can retrieve a pandas dataframe with the parameters (decay_rate, diffusion_coefficient) that were set for each substrate.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="df = mcds.get_substrate_df()
df.head()"><pre><span class="pl-s1">df</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">mcds</span>.<span class="pl-en">get_substrate_df</span>()
<span class="pl-s1">df</span>.<span class="pl-en">head</span>()</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Regarding the concentrations, we can retrieve:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>a <strong>numpy array</strong> of all substrate concentrations at a particular xyz coordinate, ordered alphabetically by substrate name, like the list retrieved by the get_substrate_names function.</li>
<li>substrate specific 3D or 2D <strong>meshgrid numpy arrays</strong>.
To get a 2D meshgrids you can slice though any z stack value, the function will always pick the closest mesh center coordinate, the smaller coordinate, if you hit the saddle point between two voxels.</li>
<li><strong>matplotlib contour and contourf plots</strong>, for any substrate, through any z_slice.</li>
<li>a <strong>pandas dataframe</strong> with voxel ijk coordinate values, mesh center mnp coordinate values, and concentrations values for all substrates.</li>
</ul>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# all concentration values at a particular coordinate
mcds.get_concentration_at(x=0, y=0, z=0)  # array([34.4166271])
mcds.get_concentration_at(x=111, y=22, z=-5)  # array([18.80652216])
mcds.get_concentration_at(x=111, y=22, z=-5.1)  # None and Warning @ pyMCDS.is_in_mesh : z = -5.1 out of bounds: z-range is (-5.0, 5.0)

oxygen_2d.shape  # (11, 11)

fig = mcds.get_contour('oxygen')
fig = mcds.get_contour('oxygen', z_slice=3.333)

df = mcds.get_concentration_df()
df.head()

df = mcds.get_concentration_df(states=2)

<span class="pl-s1">df</span>.<span class="pl-en">head</span>()  <span class="pl-c"># oxygen concentration varies over the domain</span></pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Cell (Discrete Cells) Data</h4><a id="user-content-cell-discrete-cells-data" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Cell (Discrete Cells) Data" href="#cell-discrete-cells-data"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Now, let's have a look at all variables we track from each agent.<br>
It is quite a list.<br>
This list is ordered alphabetically, except for the first entry, which always is ID.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="mcds.get_cell_variables()  # ['ID', 'attachment_elastic_constant', ..., 'velocity_z']
len(mcds.get_cell_variables())  # 77"><pre><span class="pl-s1">mcds</span>.<span class="pl-en">get_cell_variables</span>()  <span class="pl-c"># ['ID', 'attachment_elastic_constant', ..., 'velocity_z']</span>
<span class="pl-en">len</span>(<span class="pl-s1">mcds</span>.<span class="pl-en">get_cell_variables</span>())  <span class="pl-c"># 77</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">The data itself we can retrieve as dataframe.<br>
There exist two functions to do so.<br>
One that retrieves data from all agents in the whole domain, the other retrieves only data from the agents in a particular voxel, specified by the xyz coordinate.<br>
Please note, this dataframes not only hold the exact xyz coordinate, and all discrete variables mentioned above, they list additionally all agent surrounding substrate concentrations, the containing ijk voxel coordinate, and the mnp mesh center coordinate.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# data from all agents in the domain

<p dir="auto">Additionally, there is a scatter plot function available, shaped for df_cell dataframe content.</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# scatter plot
fig = mcds.get_scatter()  # default focus is cell_type and z_slice=0

<p dir="auto">Since lately, PhysiCell tracks for each cell, if this cell touches other cells.<br>
This data is stored in two dictionaries of sets of integers which link the corresponding cell IDs.<br>
We have here a closer look at the neighbor graph because the attached graph is in this particular study not really interesting.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# attached graph
graph = mcds.get_attached_graph_dict()

graph = mcds.get_neighbor_graph_dict()

graph[0]  # {1, 31, 33, 929, 935, 950}"><pre><span class="pl-c"># attached graph</span>

<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Units</h4><a id="user-content-units" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Units" href="#units"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Finally, it is possible to retrieve a pandas series that lists all units from all tracked variables, from metadata, mesh, continuum_variables, and discrete_cells.</p>

<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">MCDS Time Steps, Pandas, and Plotting</h4><a id="user-content-mcds-time-steps-pandas-and-plotting" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: MCDS Time Steps, Pandas, and Plotting" href="#mcds-time-steps-pandas-and-plotting"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Since microenvironment data and cell data can be retrieved as pandas datafarme, basic plotting (line plot, bar plot, histogram, boxplot, kernel density estimation plot, area plot, pie plot, scatter plot, hexbin plot) can easily be generated with the <strong>pandas plot function</strong>.
As mentioned above, for microenvironment data, the TimeStep class has a mcds.get_contour function because pandas has no contour and contourf plots implementation.
All these plots are <strong>mathplotlib</strong> plots, hence fine tuning can always be done using the matplotlib library.</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><a href="https://pandas.pydata.org/pandas-docs/stable/reference/api/pandas.DataFrame.plot.html" rel="nofollow">https://pandas.pydata.org/pandas-docs/stable/reference/api/pandas.DataFrame.plot.html</a></li>
<li><a href="https://matplotlib.org/" rel="nofollow">https://matplotlib.org/</a></li>
</ul>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# load library
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

# set constantes
z_slice = 0

# generate plot
fig, ax = plt.subplots(figsize=(7,4))

# plot microenvironment
mcds.get_contour('oxygen', z_slice=z_slice, ax=ax)

# plot cells
df = mcds.get_cell_df()
df = df.loc[(df.mesh_center_p == z_slice),:]
df.plot(
    kind = 'scatter',
    x = 'position_x',
    y = 'position_y',
    s = 10,
    c = 'oncoprotein',
    cmap = 'magma',
    vmin = 0,
    vmax = 2,
    grid = True,
    title = 'cells and microenvironment',
    ax = ax,
)
ax.axis('equal')
plt.tight_layout()

# save plot to file
# bue 20230101: note, in this test dataset, cells were seeded outside the actual domain.
fig.savefig('pymcds_2d_cell_and_microenvironment.png', facecolor='white')
plt.close()"><pre><span class="pl-c"># load library</span>

    <span class="pl-s1">s</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">10</span>,
    <span class="pl-s1">c</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s">'oncoprotein'</span>,
    <span class="pl-s1">cmap</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s">'magma'</span>,
