<span class="pl-s1">plt</span>.<span class="pl-en">close</span>()</pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Transform an MCDS Time Step into an AnnData Object</h4><a id="user-content-transform-an-mcds-time-step-into-an-anndata-object" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Transform an MCDS Time Step into an AnnData Object" href="#transform-an-mcds-time-step-into-an-anndata-object"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">The <a href="https://anndata.readthedocs.io/en/latest/" rel="nofollow">AnnData</a> format is the de facto standard for single cell data analysis in python.<br>
It is a one-liner to transform a mcds object onto an anndata object.<br>
This is the gate to a whole new universe.</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><a href="https://scverse.org/" rel="nofollow">https://scverse.org/</a></li>
</ul>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="ann = mcds.get_anndata()
print(ann)  # AnnData object with n_obs × n_vars = 1099 × 80
            #     obs: 'ID', 'current_phase', 'cycle_model'
            #     obsm: 'spatial'"><pre><span class="pl-s1">ann</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">mcds</span>.<span class="pl-en">get_anndata</span>()
<span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s1">ann</span>)  <span class="pl-c"># AnnData object with n_obs × n_vars = 1099 × 80</span>
            <span class="pl-c">#     obs: 'ID', 'current_phase', 'cycle_model'</span>
            <span class="pl-c">#     obsm: 'spatial'</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">The output tells us that we have loaded a time step  with 1099 cells (agents) and 80 features.
And that we have spatial coordinate annotation (position_x, position_y, position_z, time) of the loaded data.</p>
<p dir="auto">Whatever you d'like to do with your physicell data, it most probably was already done with single cell wet lab data.
That's being said: PhysiCell data is different scdata than scRNA seq, for example.
scRNA seq data is higher dimensional (e.g. for the human genome, over 20000 genes each time step) than PhysiCell data (tens, maybe hundreds of features).
scRNA seq data is always single time step data because the measurement consumes the sample.
PhysiCell data is always time series data, even we look at this moment only at one time step.
This all means, the wet lab bioinformatics will partially try to solve problems (e.g. trajectory inference), that simply are no problems for us and the other way around.</p>
<p dir="auto">Anyhow, the gate is open.
For the shake of appearances, let's do a cluster analysis on PhysiCell output using scanpy.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="import scanpy as sc

# loads only feature that have not the same value in all cells.
# max absolute scales the features into a range between -1 and 1.
ann = mcds.get_anndata(states=2, scale='maxabs')

# principal component analysis
sc.tl.pca(ann)  # process anndata object with the pca tool.
sc.pl.pca(ann)  # plot pca result.
ann.var_names  # list the numerical features we have at hand (alternative way: ann.var.index).
ann.obs_keys()  # list the categories features we have at hand (alternative way: ann.obs.columns).
sc.pl.pca(ann, color=['current_phase','oxygen'])  # plot the pca results colored by some features.
sc.pl.pca(ann, color=list(ann.var_names)+list(ann.obs_keys()))  # gotta catch 'em all!
sc.pl.pca_variance_ratio(ann)  # plot how much of the variation each principal component captures.

# neighborhood graph clustering
sc.pp.neighbors(ann, n_neighbors=15)  # compute the neighborhood graph with the neighbors preprocess step.
sc.tl.leiden(ann, resolution=0.01)  # cluster the neighborhood graph with the leiden tool.
sc.pl.pca(ann, color='leiden')  # plot the pca results colored by leiden clusters.

# umap dimensional reduction embedding
sc.tl.umap(ann)  # process anndata object with the umap tool.
sc.pl.umap(ann, color=['current_phase','oxygen','leiden'])  # plot the umap result colored by some features."><pre><span class="pl-k">import</span> <span class="pl-s1">scanpy</span> <span class="pl-k">as</span> <span class="pl-s1">sc</span>

<span class="pl-c"># loads only feature that have not the same value in all cells.</span>
<span class="pl-c"># max absolute scales the features into a range between -1 and 1.</span>
<span class="pl-s1">ann</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">mcds</span>.<span class="pl-en">get_anndata</span>(<span class="pl-s1">states</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-c1">2</span>, <span class="pl-s1">scale</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-s">'maxabs'</span>)

<span class="pl-c"># principal component analysis</span>
<span class="pl-s1">sc</span>.<span class="pl-s1">tl</span>.<span class="pl-en">pca</span>(<span class="pl-s1">ann</span>)  <span class="pl-c"># process anndata object with the pca tool.</span>
<span class="pl-s1">sc</span>.<span class="pl-s1">pl</span>.<span class="pl-en">pca</span>(<span class="pl-s1">ann</span>)  <span class="pl-c"># plot pca result.</span>
<span class="pl-s1">ann</span>.<span class="pl-s1">var_names</span>  <span class="pl-c"># list the numerical features we have at hand (alternative way: ann.var.index).</span>
<span class="pl-s1">ann</span>.<span class="pl-en">obs_keys</span>()  <span class="pl-c"># list the categories features we have at hand (alternative way: ann.obs.columns).</span>
<span class="pl-s1">sc</span>.<span class="pl-s1">pl</span>.<span class="pl-en">pca</span>(<span class="pl-s1">ann</span>, <span class="pl-s1">color</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span>[<span class="pl-s">'current_phase'</span>,<span class="pl-s">'oxygen'</span>])  <span class="pl-c"># plot the pca results colored by some features.</span>
<span class="pl-s1">sc</span>.<span class="pl-s1">pl</span>.<span class="pl-en">pca</span>(<span class="pl-s1">ann</span>, <span class="pl-s1">color</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-en">list</span>(<span class="pl-s1">ann</span>.<span class="pl-s1">var_names</span>)<span class="pl-c1">+</span><span class="pl-en">list</span>(<span class="pl-s1">ann</span>.<span class="pl-en">obs_keys</span>()))  <span class="pl-c"># gotta catch 'em all!</span>
<span class="pl-s1">sc</span>.<span class="pl-s1">pl</span>.<span class="pl-en">pca_variance_ratio</span>(<span class="pl-s1">ann</span>)  <span class="pl-c"># plot how much of the variation each principal component captures.</span>

<span class="pl-c"># neighborhood graph clustering</span>
<span class="pl-s1">sc</span>.<span class="pl-s1">pp</span>.<span class="pl-en">neighbors</span>(<span class="pl-s1">ann</span>, <span class="pl-s1">n_neighbors</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-c1">15</span>)  <span class="pl-c"># compute the neighborhood graph with the neighbors preprocess step.</span>
<span class="pl-s1">sc</span>.<span class="pl-s1">tl</span>.<span class="pl-en">leiden</span>(<span class="pl-s1">ann</span>, <span class="pl-s1">resolution</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-c1">0.01</span>)  <span class="pl-c"># cluster the neighborhood graph with the leiden tool.</span>
<span class="pl-s1">sc</span>.<span class="pl-s1">pl</span>.<span class="pl-en">pca</span>(<span class="pl-s1">ann</span>, <span class="pl-s1">color</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-s">'leiden'</span>)  <span class="pl-c"># plot the pca results colored by leiden clusters.</span>

<span class="pl-c"># umap dimensional reduction embedding</span>
<span class="pl-s1">sc</span>.<span class="pl-s1">tl</span>.<span class="pl-en">umap</span>(<span class="pl-s1">ann</span>)  <span class="pl-c"># process anndata object with the umap tool.</span>
<span class="pl-s1">sc</span>.<span class="pl-s1">pl</span>.<span class="pl-en">umap</span>(<span class="pl-s1">ann</span>, <span class="pl-s1">color</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span>[<span class="pl-s">'current_phase'</span>,<span class="pl-s">'oxygen'</span>,<span class="pl-s">'leiden'</span>])  <span class="pl-c"># plot the umap result colored by some features.</span></pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Working With MCDS Time Series in Python3</h3><a id="user-content-working-with-mcds-time-series-in-python3" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Working With MCDS Time Series in Python3" href="#working-with-mcds-time-series-in-python3"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">An exciting thing about modeling is to have time series data.<br>
Pcdl's TimeSeries class is here to make the handling of a time series of MCD snapshots easy.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="import pathlib  # library to locate the test data
import pcdl  # the physicell data loader library

s_path = str(pathlib.Path(pcdl.__file__).parent.joinpath('data_timeseries_2d'))  # local path to the installed test data set
print('mcds time series:', s_path)

# generate a mcds time series instance
mcdsts = pcdl.TimeSeries(s_path)"><pre><span class="pl-k">import</span> <span class="pl-s1">pathlib</span>  <span class="pl-c"># library to locate the test data</span>
<span class="pl-k">import</span> <span class="pl-s1">pcdl</span>  <span class="pl-c"># the physicell data loader library</span>

<span class="pl-s1">s_path</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-en">str</span>(<span class="pl-s1">pathlib</span>.<span class="pl-v">Path</span>(<span class="pl-s1">pcdl</span>.<span class="pl-s1">__file__</span>).<span class="pl-s1">parent</span>.<span class="pl-en">joinpath</span>(<span class="pl-s">'data_timeseries_2d'</span>))  <span class="pl-c"># local path to the installed test data set</span>
<span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">'mcds time series:'</span>, <span class="pl-s1">s_path</span>)

<span class="pl-c"># generate a mcds time series instance</span>
<span class="pl-s1">mcdsts</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">pcdl</span>.<span class="pl-v">TimeSeries</span>(<span class="pl-s1">s_path</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Like in the pyMCDs class, for memory consumption and processing speed control, we can specify if we want to load microenvironment data and graph data from the snapshots we later on analyze.<br>
By default, all data related to the snapshot is loaded, if needed, we can set load to False.<br>
Additionally, we can exclude to read the PhysiCell_settings.xml file, if it is not available, and fine tune variable typing.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# fine tuned the way mcds objects will be loaded
mcdsts = pcdl.TimeSeries(s_path, custom_type={}, load=True, microenv=False, graph=False, settingxml=None)"><pre><span class="pl-c"># fine tuned the way mcds objects will be loaded</span>
<span class="pl-s1">mcdsts</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">pcdl</span>.<span class="pl-v">TimeSeries</span>(<span class="pl-s1">s_path</span>, <span class="pl-s1">custom_type</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span>{}, <span class="pl-s1">load</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-c1">True</span>, <span class="pl-s1">microenv</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-c1">False</span>, <span class="pl-s1">graph</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-c1">False</span>, <span class="pl-s1">settingxml</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-c1">None</span>)</pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">MCDS Times Series Data Analysis - the Basics</h4><a id="user-content-mcds-times-series-data-analysis---the-basics" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: MCDS Times Series Data Analysis - the Basics" href="#mcds-times-series-data-analysis---the-basics"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Now, let's have a look at the TimeSeries instances data analysis functions.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# fetch data
mcdsts = pcdl.TimeSeries(s_path, load=False)"><pre><span class="pl-c"># fetch data</span>
<span class="pl-s1">mcdsts</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">pcdl</span>.<span class="pl-v">TimeSeries</span>(<span class="pl-s1">s_path</span>, <span class="pl-s1">load</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-c1">False</span>)</pre></div>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><strong>get_xmlfile_list</strong> will simply return a list of absolute path and mcds xml file name strings.<br>
This list can be manipulated, and later be fed into the objects read_xml function, to only read specific snapshots into memory.
For example, if you want only to analyze hour 11, 12, and 13 from your run, or if data from every other hour will be enough.</li>
</ul>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="ls_xml = mcdsts.get_xmlfile_list()
ls_xml   # ['/path/to/output00000000.xml', '/path/to/output00000001.xml', ..., '/path/to/output00000024.xml']

# filter for snapshot 11,12, and 13
ls_xml_11_12_13 = ls_xml[11:14]
ls_xml_11_12_13  # ['/path/to/output00000011.xml', '/path/to/output00000012.xml', '/path/to/output00000013.xml']

# filter for every other snapshot
ls_xml_even = [s_xml for i, s_xml in enumerate(ls_xml) if (i%2 == 0)]
ls_xml_even  # ['/path/to/output00000000.xml', '/path/to/output00000002.xml', ..., /path/to/output00000024.xml']"><pre><span class="pl-s1">ls_xml</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">mcdsts</span>.<span class="pl-en">get_xmlfile_list</span>()
<span class="pl-s1">ls_xml</span>   <span class="pl-c"># ['/path/to/output00000000.xml', '/path/to/output00000001.xml', ..., '/path/to/output00000024.xml']</span>

<span class="pl-c"># filter for snapshot 11,12, and 13</span>
<span class="pl-s1">ls_xml_11_12_13</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">ls_xml</span>[<span class="pl-c1">11</span>:<span class="pl-c1">14</span>]
<span class="pl-s1">ls_xml_11_12_13</span>  <span class="pl-c"># ['/path/to/output00000011.xml', '/path/to/output00000012.xml', '/path/to/output00000013.xml']</span>

<span class="pl-c"># filter for every other snapshot</span>
<span class="pl-s1">ls_xml_even</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> [<span class="pl-s1">s_xml</span> <span class="pl-k">for</span> <span class="pl-s1">i</span>, <span class="pl-s1">s_xml</span> <span class="pl-c1">in</span> <span class="pl-en">enumerate</span>(<span class="pl-s1">ls_xml</span>) <span class="pl-k">if</span> (<span class="pl-s1">i</span><span class="pl-c1">%</span><span class="pl-c1">2</span> <span class="pl-c1">==</span> <span class="pl-c1">0</span>)]
<span class="pl-s1">ls_xml_even</span>  <span class="pl-c"># ['/path/to/output00000000.xml', '/path/to/output00000002.xml', ..., /path/to/output00000024.xml']</span></pre></div>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><strong>read_xml</strong> will actually read the snapshots into RAM.<br>
The default setting will read all snapshots from a time series. <br>
However, you can always use a filtered ls_xml list to only load a subset of snapshots.</li>
</ul>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# load all snapshots
mcdsts.read_mcds()
mcdsts.get_mcds_list()  # YMMV! [&lt;pcdl.pyMCDS.pyMCDS at 0x7fa660996b00&gt;, &lt;pcdl.pyMCDS.pyMCDS at 0x7fa67673e1d0&gt;, ..., &lt;pcdl.pyMCDS.pyMCDS at 0x7fa660950f10&gt;]
len(mcdsts.get_mcds_list())  # 25

# load snapshot 11, 12, and 13
mcdsts.read_mcds(ls_xml_11_12_13)
len(mcdsts.get_mcds_list())  # 3

# load all even snapshots
mcdsts.read_mcds(ls_xml_even)
len(mcdsts.get_mcds_list())  # 13"><pre><span class="pl-c"># load all snapshots</span>
<span class="pl-s1">mcdsts</span>.<span class="pl-en">read_mcds</span>()
<span class="pl-s1">mcdsts</span>.<span class="pl-en">get_mcds_list</span>()  <span class="pl-c"># YMMV! [&lt;pcdl.pyMCDS.pyMCDS at 0x7fa660996b00&gt;, &lt;pcdl.pyMCDS.pyMCDS at 0x7fa67673e1d0&gt;, ..., &lt;pcdl.pyMCDS.pyMCDS at 0x7fa660950f10&gt;]</span>
<span class="pl-en">len</span>(<span class="pl-s1">mcdsts</span>.<span class="pl-en">get_mcds_list</span>())  <span class="pl-c"># 25</span>

<span class="pl-c"># load snapshot 11, 12, and 13</span>
<span class="pl-s1">mcdsts</span>.<span class="pl-en">read_mcds</span>(<span class="pl-s1">ls_xml_11_12_13</span>)
<span class="pl-en">len</span>(<span class="pl-s1">mcdsts</span>.<span class="pl-en">get_mcds_list</span>())  <span class="pl-c"># 3</span>

<span class="pl-c"># load all even snapshots</span>
<span class="pl-s1">mcdsts</span>.<span class="pl-en">read_mcds</span>(<span class="pl-s1">ls_xml_even</span>)
<span class="pl-en">len</span>(<span class="pl-s1">mcdsts</span>.<span class="pl-en">get_mcds_list</span>())  <span class="pl-c"># 13</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Single snapshots can now be accessed by indexing.<br>
With a single snapshot, you work exactly in the same way as with an object loaded by TimeStep.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# get the simulation time
mcdsts.get_mcds_list()[12].get_time()  # 720.0

# get the cell data frame
df = mcdsts.get_mcds_list()[12].get_cell_df()
df.shape  # (992, 87)
df.head()"><pre><span class="pl-c"># get the simulation time</span>
<span class="pl-s1">mcdsts</span>.<span class="pl-en">get_mcds_list</span>()[<span class="pl-c1">12</span>].<span class="pl-en">get_time</span>()  <span class="pl-c"># 720.0</span>

<span class="pl-c"># get the cell data frame</span>
<span class="pl-s1">df</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">mcdsts</span>.<span class="pl-en">get_mcds_list</span>()[<span class="pl-c1">12</span>].<span class="pl-en">get_cell_df</span>()
<span class="pl-s1">df</span>.<span class="pl-s1">shape</span>  <span class="pl-c"># (992, 87)</span>
<span class="pl-s1">df</span>.<span class="pl-en">head</span>()</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">It is very easy to loop over the whole time series, to analyze time series data, and generate time series plots.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# load library
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt
import pandas as pd

# fetch data
mcdsts = pcdl.TimeSeries(s_path)

# loop over the time series to gather temporal information like, for example, data for a growth curve
lr_time = [mcds.get_time() for mcds in mcdsts.get_mcds_list()]  # [0.0, 60.0, ..., 1440.0]
li_cellcount = [mcds.get_cell_df().shape[0] for mcds in mcdsts.get_mcds_list()]  # [889, 898, ..., 1099]

# pack data into a pandas datafarm
df = pd.DataFrame([lr_time,li_cellcount], index=['time_min','cell_count']).T
df.head()

# plot data
df.plot(
    kind = 'scatter',
    x = 'time_min',
    y = 'cell_count',
    s = 36,
    ylim = (800,1200),
    grid=True,
    title='2D time series test data'
)

# save plot to file
fig, ax = plt.subplots()
df.plot(
    kind = 'scatter',
    x = 'time_min',
    y = 'cell_count',
    s = 36,
    ylim = (800,1200),
    grid = True,
    title = '2D time series test data',
    ax = ax,
)
plt.tight_layout()
fig.savefig('pymcdsts_2d_cellcount.png', facecolor='white')
plt.close()"><pre><span class="pl-c"># load library</span>

<span class="pl-s1">fig</span>.<span class="pl-en">savefig</span>(<span class="pl-s">'pymcdsts_2d_cellcount.png'</span>, <span class="pl-s1">facecolor</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-s">'white'</span>)
<span class="pl-s1">plt</span>.<span class="pl-en">close</span>()</pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Times Series Data Scatter Plot Images, Contour Plot Images, and Movies</h4><a id="user-content-times-series-data-scatter-plot-images-contour-plot-images-and-movies" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Times Series Data Scatter Plot Images, Contour Plot Images, and Movies" href="#times-series-data-scatter-plot-images-contour-plot-images-and-movies"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">With PhysiCell it is not only possible to take data snapshots, but as well <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SVG" rel="nofollow">svg</a> vector graphics images snapshots.<br>
PhysiCell's <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Make_(software)" rel="nofollow">Makefile</a> has code to translate those svg images into <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GIF" rel="nofollow">gif</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/JPEG" rel="nofollow">jpeg</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Portable_Network_Graphics" rel="nofollow">png</a>, or <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TIFF" rel="nofollow">tiff</a> format, making use of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ImageMagick" rel="nofollow">image magick</a> library.
The Makefile also has  code to translate the jpeg, png, or tiff images into a <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MP4_file_format" rel="nofollow">mp4</a> movie, therefore utilizing the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FFmpeg" rel="nofollow">ffmpeg</a> library.<br>
TimeSeries instances provide similar functionality, although the jpeg, png, and tiff images are generated straight from data and not from the svg files.
However, mp4 movies and gif images are generated in the same way.
This means the mcdsts.make_gif code will only run if image magick and mcdsts.make_movie code will only run if ffmpeg is installed on your computer.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# fetch data
mcdsts = pcdl.TimeSeries(s_path)"><pre><span class="pl-c"># fetch data</span>
<span class="pl-s1">mcdsts</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">pcdl</span>.<span class="pl-v">TimeSeries</span>(<span class="pl-s1">s_path</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Translate physicell output data into static raster graphic images:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# cell images colored by cell_type
mcdsts.make_imgcell()  # jpeg images colored by cell_type
mcdsts.make_imgcell(ext='png')  # png images colored by cell_type
mcdsts.make_imgcell(ext='tiff')  # tiff images colored by cell_type

# cell images can be colored by any cell dataframe column, like, for example, by pressure
# there are parameters to adjust cell size and more
mcdsts.make_imgcell(focus='pressure')  # jpeg images colored by pressure values

# substrate data owns an equivalent function,
# being able to display any substrate dataframe column
mcdsts.make_imgconc(focus='oxygen')  # jpeg images colored by oxygen values"><pre><span class="pl-c"># cell images colored by cell_type</span>
<span class="pl-s1">mcdsts</span>.<span class="pl-en">make_imgcell</span>()  <span class="pl-c"># jpeg images colored by cell_type</span>
<span class="pl-s1">mcdsts</span>.<span class="pl-en">make_imgcell</span>(<span class="pl-s1">ext</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-s">'png'</span>)  <span class="pl-c"># png images colored by cell_type</span>
<span class="pl-s1">mcdsts</span>.<span class="pl-en">make_imgcell</span>(<span class="pl-s1">ext</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-s">'tiff'</span>)  <span class="pl-c"># tiff images colored by cell_type</span>

<span class="pl-c"># cell images can be colored by any cell dataframe column, like, for example, by pressure</span>
<span class="pl-c"># there are parameters to adjust cell size and more</span>
<span class="pl-s1">mcdsts</span>.<span class="pl-en">make_imgcell</span>(<span class="pl-s1">focus</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-s">'pressure'</span>)  <span class="pl-c"># jpeg images colored by pressure values</span>

<span class="pl-c"># substrate data owns an equivalent function,</span>
<span class="pl-c"># being able to display any substrate dataframe column</span>
<span class="pl-s1">mcdsts</span>.<span class="pl-en">make_imgconc</span>(<span class="pl-s1">focus</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-s">'oxygen'</span>)  <span class="pl-c"># jpeg images colored by oxygen values</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Translate raster graphic images into a dynamic gif image:<br>
Gif images can only be generated for already existing jpeg, png, or tiff images!<br>
By default, jpeg files will be used, to generate the gif.<br>
If png or tiff files should be used as source, then this has to be explicitly stated.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# using jpeg images for input
s_path = mcdsts.make_imgcell()
mcdsts.make_gif(s_path)

# using jpeg images one-liner
mcdsts.make_gif(mcdsts.make_imgcell())

# using tiff images for input
s_path = mcdsts.make_imgcell(ext='tiff')
mcdsts.make_gif(s_path, interface='tiff')"><pre><span class="pl-c"># using jpeg images for input</span>
<span class="pl-s1">s_path</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">mcdsts</span>.<span class="pl-en">make_imgcell</span>()
<span class="pl-s1">mcdsts</span>.<span class="pl-en">make_gif</span>(<span class="pl-s1">s_path</span>)

<span class="pl-c"># using jpeg images one-liner</span>
<span class="pl-s1">mcdsts</span>.<span class="pl-en">make_gif</span>(<span class="pl-s1">mcdsts</span>.<span class="pl-en">make_imgcell</span>())

<span class="pl-c"># using tiff images for input</span>
<span class="pl-s1">s_path</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">mcdsts</span>.<span class="pl-en">make_imgcell</span>(<span class="pl-s1">ext</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-s">'tiff'</span>)
<span class="pl-s1">mcdsts</span>.<span class="pl-en">make_gif</span>(<span class="pl-s1">s_path</span>, <span class="pl-s1">interface</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-s">'tiff'</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Translate raster graphic images into an mp4 movie:<br>
Movies can only be generated for already existing jpeg, png, or tiff images!</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# using jpeg images for input
s_path = mcdsts.make_imgcell()
mcdsts.make_movie(s_path)

# using jpeg images one-liner
mcdsts.make_movie(mcdsts.make_imgcell())

# using tiff images for input
s_path = mcdsts.make_imgcell(ext='tiff')
mcdsts.make_movie(s_path, interface='tiff')"><pre><span class="pl-c"># using jpeg images for input</span>
<span class="pl-s1">s_path</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">mcdsts</span>.<span class="pl-en">make_imgcell</span>()
<span class="pl-s1">mcdsts</span>.<span class="pl-en">make_movie</span>(<span class="pl-s1">s_path</span>)

<span class="pl-c"># using jpeg images one-liner</span>
<span class="pl-s1">mcdsts</span>.<span class="pl-en">make_movie</span>(<span class="pl-s1">mcdsts</span>.<span class="pl-en">make_imgcell</span>())

<span class="pl-c"># using tiff images for input</span>
<span class="pl-s1">s_path</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">mcdsts</span>.<span class="pl-en">make_imgcell</span>(<span class="pl-s1">ext</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-s">'tiff'</span>)
<span class="pl-s1">mcdsts</span>.<span class="pl-en">make_movie</span>(<span class="pl-s1">s_path</span>, <span class="pl-s1">interface</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-s">'tiff'</span>)</pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">MCDS Times Series Data Triage</h4><a id="user-content-mcds-times-series-data-triage" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: MCDS Times Series Data Triage" href="#mcds-times-series-data-triage"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Cell variables that have no variance, zero entropy, that are in all agent overall time steps in the same state, have always exacted the same value, carry no information.
Similarly, substrates variables that over the whole domain overall time steps have the same concentration are not interesting.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# fetch data
mcdsts = pcdl.TimeSeries(s_path)"><pre><span class="pl-c"># fetch data</span>
<span class="pl-s1">mcdsts</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">pcdl</span>.<span class="pl-v">TimeSeries</span>(<span class="pl-s1">s_path</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">There are functions to help triage over the entier time series for features that more likely might carry information, by checking for variables with variation.</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# cell data min max values
dl_cell = mcdsts.get_cell_df_states()  # returns a dictionary with all features, listing all accessed states
len(dl_cell)  # 84 features
dl_cell.keys()  # list feature names
dl_cell['oxygen']  # list min and max oxygen values found, surrounding a cell, over the whole series

# cell data number of states
di_state = {}
[di_state.update({s_feature: len(li_state)}) for s_feature, li_state in mcdsts.get_cell_df_states(allvalues=True).items()]
di_state['oxygen']  # cell surrounding oxygen was found occupying 2388 different states (values) over the whole time series

# substrate data
dl_conc = mcdsts.get_conc_df_states()
dl_conc.keys()  # list feature names
dl_conc['oxygen']  # list min and max oxygen values found in the domain over the whole series"><pre class="notranslate"><code># cell data min max values
dl_cell = mcdsts.get_cell_df_states()  # returns a dictionary with all features, listing all accessed states
len(dl_cell)  # 84 features
dl_cell.keys()  # list feature names
dl_cell['oxygen']  # list min and max oxygen values found, surrounding a cell, over the whole series

# cell data number of states
di_state = {}
[di_state.update({s_feature: len(li_state)}) for s_feature, li_state in mcdsts.get_cell_df_states(allvalues=True).items()]
di_state['oxygen']  # cell surrounding oxygen was found occupying 2388 different states (values) over the whole time series

# substrate data
dl_conc = mcdsts.get_conc_df_states()
dl_conc.keys()  # list feature names
dl_conc['oxygen']  # list min and max oxygen values found in the domain over the whole series
</code></pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Transform MCDS Time Series into AnnData Objects</h4><a id="user-content-transform-mcds-time-series-into-anndata-objects" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Transform MCDS Time Series into AnnData Objects" href="#transform-mcds-time-series-into-anndata-objects"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# fetch data
mcdsts = pcdl.TimeSeries(s_path)"><pre><span class="pl-c"># fetch data</span>
<span class="pl-s1">mcdsts</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">pcdl</span>.<span class="pl-v">TimeSeries</span>(<span class="pl-s1">s_path</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">A mcds time series can be translated into one single anndata (default).</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="ann = mcdsts.get_anndata(states=2, scale='maxabs', collapse=True)
print(ann)  # AnnData object with n_obs × n_vars = 889 × 26
            #     obs: 'z_layer', 'time', 'current_phase', 'cycle_model'
            #     obsm: 'spatial'"><pre><span class="pl-s1">ann</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">mcdsts</span>.<span class="pl-en">get_anndata</span>(<span class="pl-s1">states</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-c1">2</span>, <span class="pl-s1">scale</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-s">'maxabs'</span>, <span class="pl-s1">collapse</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-c1">True</span>)
<span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s1">ann</span>)  <span class="pl-c"># AnnData object with n_obs × n_vars = 889 × 26</span>
            <span class="pl-c">#     obs: 'z_layer', 'time', 'current_phase', 'cycle_model'</span>
            <span class="pl-c">#     obsm: 'spatial'</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">The output tells us that we have loaded a time series with 24758 cell (agent) snapshots and 27 features.
And that we have spatial coordinate annotation (position_x, position_y, position_z, time) of the loaded data.</p>
<p dir="auto">A mcds time series can be translated into a chronological list of anndata objects, where each entry is a single time step.
After running get_anndata, you can access the objects by the get_annmcds_list function.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="l_ann = mcdsts.get_anndata(states=2, scale='maxabs', collapse=False)
len(l_ann)  # 25
l_ann[24]  # AnnData object with n_obs × n_vars = 1099 × 79
           #     obs: 'z_layer', 'time', 'cell_type', 'current_death_model', 'current_phase', 'cycle_model'
           #     obsm: 'spatial'

# load all snapshots
mcdsts.get_annmcds_list()  # YMMV! [AnnData object with n_obs × n_vars ..., ..., ... obsm: 'spatial']
len(mcdsts.get_annmcds_list())  # 25"><pre><span class="pl-s1">l_ann</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">mcdsts</span>.<span class="pl-en">get_anndata</span>(<span class="pl-s1">states</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-c1">2</span>, <span class="pl-s1">scale</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-s">'maxabs'</span>, <span class="pl-s1">collapse</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-c1">False</span>)
<span class="pl-en">len</span>(<span class="pl-s1">l_ann</span>)  <span class="pl-c"># 25</span>
<span class="pl-s1">l_ann</span>[<span class="pl-c1">24</span>]  <span class="pl-c"># AnnData object with n_obs × n_vars = 1099 × 79</span>
           <span class="pl-c">#     obs: 'z_layer', 'time', 'cell_type', 'current_death_model', 'current_phase', 'cycle_model'</span>
           <span class="pl-c">#     obsm: 'spatial'</span>

<span class="pl-c"># load all snapshots</span>
<span class="pl-s1">mcdsts</span>.<span class="pl-en">get_annmcds_list</span>()  <span class="pl-c"># YMMV! [AnnData object with n_obs × n_vars ..., ..., ... obsm: 'spatial']</span>
<span class="pl-en">len</span>(<span class="pl-s1">mcdsts</span>.<span class="pl-en">get_annmcds_list</span>())  <span class="pl-c"># 25</span></pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Data Clean Up</h3><a id="user-content-data-clean-up" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Data Clean Up" href="#data-clean-up"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">After you are done checking out the results, you can uninstall the test datasets and all files stored within its folders.</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="pcdl.uninstall_data()"><pre class="notranslate"><code>pcdl.uninstall_data()
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>That's all Folks!</strong></p>
